{"step_index":108,"source":"USER_EXPLICIT","type":"USER_INPUT","status":"DONE","created_at":"2026-07-17T13:15:30Z","content":"<USER_REQUEST>\nInternal Admin Console – Detailed Implementation Plan for IEP\n1. Overview\n\nAs the Interactive Engagement Platform (IEP) grows and starts supporting more users and organizations, managing customer accounts, events, integrations, and technical issues directly through the database will become difficult and risky.\n\nWe propose building a separate Internal Admin Console for the IEP team.\n\nThe existing platform will effectively have three interfaces:\n\nIEP Platform\n│\n├── Participant Experience\n│   └── Join events and participate in Polls, Quizzes,\n│       Q&A, Surveys, Feedback and Word Clouds\n│\n├── Host Dashboard\n│   └── Create and manage events, activities,\n│       analytics, AI Studio and integrations\n│\n└── Internal Admin Console\n    └── Manage and support the entire IEP platform\n\nThe Admin Console will only be accessible to authorized internal team members.\n\nThe primary goal is to allow the support and operations teams to:\n\nFind and troubleshoot customer accounts.\nMonitor events.\nInvestigate integration problems.\nManage organizations and users.\nView platform-wide analytics.\nInvestigate errors and support issues.\nMonitor platform and integration health.\nPerform controlled administrative actions.\nMaintain an audit trail of sensitive operations.\n\nThis removes the need for support staff to directly access MongoDB or ask developers to investigate routine customer issues.\n\n2. Proposed Technical Architecture\n\nSince IEP already uses a Turborepo architecture, the Admin Console can be introduced as a separate frontend application.\n\ninteractive-engagement-app/\n│\n├── apps/\n│   │\n│   ├── web/\n│   │   └── Existing Host + Participant application\n│   │\n│   ├── admin/\n│   │   └── New Internal Admin Console\n│   │\n│   └── api/\n│       └── Existing NestJS Backend\n│\n└── packages/\n    ├── ui/\n    ├── types/\n    └── shared/\n\nWe will not initially create a completely separate backend.\n\nThe architecture would be:\n\n                    Auth0\n                      │\n                      ▼\n              Admin Authentication\n                      │\n                      ▼\n              ┌───────────────┐\n              │   Admin App   │\n              │    Next.js    │\n              └───────┬───────┘\n                      │\n                      │ Admin APIs\n                      ▼\n              ┌───────────────┐\n              │  NestJS API   │\n              │ /api/admin/*  │\n              └───────┬───────┘\n                      │\n          ┌───────────┼───────────┐\n          ▼           ▼           ▼\n       MongoDB       Redis     Socket.IO\n          │\n          └───────────┬───────────┐\n                      ▼           ▼\n                AI Services   Integrations\n                              Zoom\n                              Teams\n                              Google Meet\n\nThis approach allows us to reuse the existing backend services while maintaining a clear separation between customer-facing and internal administrative functionality.\n\n3. Authentication and Authorization\n\nSecurity should be the first implementation priority because the Admin Console will have access to sensitive platform-wide information.\n\nWe should define multiple roles.\n\nPlatform Admin\n    │\n    ├── Full platform access\n    │\n    ├── Manage users\n    ├── Manage organizations\n    ├── Manage events\n    ├── Change feature flags\n    └── Administrative actions\n\n\nSupport Agent\n    │\n    ├── Search customers\n    ├── View events\n    ├── View integration status\n    └── Troubleshoot issues\n\n\nOperations\n    │\n    ├── Platform analytics\n    ├── System health\n    └── Usage monitoring\n\n\nCustomer Success\n    │\n    ├── Organizations\n    ├── Plans\n    ├── Usage\n    └── Account information\n\nInitially, we can start with fewer roles, such as:\n\nhost\nadmin\n\nLater, the permission system can evolve into:\n\nhost\nsupport\noperations\nadmin\nsuper_admin\n\nEvery Admin API request should pass through:\n\nRequest\n   ↓\nJWT Validation\n   ↓\nAuthentication Guard\n   ↓\nRole/Permission Guard\n   ↓\nAdmin API\n   ↓\nService\n   ↓\nDatabase\n\nSimply hiding admin pages in the frontend is not enough. Authorization must always be enforced by the NestJS backend.\n\n4. Phase 1 – Admin Foundation\n\nThe first development phase establishes the Admin Console itself.\n\nFrontend\n\nCreate:\n\napps/admin\n\nTechnology:\n\nNext.js\nTypeScript\nTailwind\nExisting IEP design system where practical\n\nInitial layout:\n\nAdmin Console\n\nDashboard\n\nOrganizations\n\nUsers\n\nEvents\n\nIntegrations\n\nSupport\n\nAnalytics\n\nAudit Logs\n\nModeration\n\nSystem Health\n\nSettings\nBackend\n\nCreate an Admin domain:\n\napps/api/src/admin/\n\nadmin.module.ts\n\nadmin.controller.ts\n\nadmin.service.ts\n\nAdmin routes will be isolated under a dedicated prefix, for example:\n\n/api/admin/*\n\nThe goal of Phase 1 is not to implement every feature. It creates the secure foundation on which future modules can be added.\n\n5. Phase 2 – User Management\n\nThis will likely be one of the most frequently used areas for client support.\n\nThe Admin Console should provide global user search.\n\nAdministrators should be able to search using:\n\nEmail\nName\nUser ID\nAuth0 ID\n\nOpening a user should display:\n\nUser Profile\n\nName\nEmail\nUser ID\nAuth0 ID\n\nRole\n\nOrganization\n\nAccount Status\n\nCreated Date\n\nLast Login\n\nPlan\n\nAI Usage\n\nRecent Events\n\nConnected Integrations\n\nFrom here, authorized administrators could perform controlled operations such as:\n\nSuspend account.\nReactivate account.\nReset selected usage quotas.\nView recent events.\nCheck integration status.\n\nDangerous actions must require confirmation.\n\nFor example:\n\nSuspend User\n\nAre you sure you want to suspend this account?\n\nReason:\n[________________________]\n\nCancel          Confirm\n\nThe reason and administrator identity should then be stored in the Audit Log.\n\n6. Phase 3 – Organization Management\n\nAs IEP moves toward enterprise customers, individual users should eventually belong to organizations.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganization\n\nABC Corporation\n\nPlan\nEnterprise\n\nUsers\n250\n\nEvents\n4,520\n\nActive Events\n12\n\nAI Usage\n45,230 requests\n\nIntegrations\n\nZoom        Connected\nTeams       Connected\nGoogle Meet Connected\n\nOrganization management would allow internal teams to understand the complete customer account rather than looking at individual users separately.\n\nThe organization detail page could contain:\n\nOverview\n\nUsers\n\nEvents\n\nUsage\n\nIntegrations\n\nFeatures\n\nAudit History\n\nThis will become particularly important for enterprise customers.\n\n7. Phase 4 – Event Troubleshooting\n\nThis should be one of the core client-support capabilities.\n\nSuppose a customer reports:\n\n\"Our poll is stuck during a live event.\"\n\nThe support agent should be able to search:\n\nEvent Code: ABC123\n\nThe Admin Console retrieves:\n\nEvent\n\nAnnual Conference\n\nStatus\nLIVE\n\nHost\ncustomer@example.com\n\nParticipants\n1,250\n\nActive Activity\nPoll #4\n\nSocket Connections\n1,203\n\nCreated\n10:00 AM\n\nThe support agent could then inspect:\n\nEvent\n   │\n   ├── Activities\n   ├── Participants\n   ├── Analytics\n   ├── Realtime State\n   ├── Integrations\n   └── Audit Timeline\n\nInitially, administrative intervention should be limited to safe actions such as:\n\nForce-end event.\nClear invalid active activity state.\nInspect event configuration.\n\nMore powerful actions should only be added when there is a demonstrated support requirement.\n\n8. Phase 5 – Integration Management\n\nBecause IEP integrates with:\n\nZoom\nMicrosoft Teams\nGoogle Meet\n\nintegration troubleshooting should have its own module.\n\nThe Admin Console could display:\n\nIntegration Health\n\nZoom\nStatus: Connected\nOAuth: Valid\nLast Sync: 10 minutes ago\n\nMicrosoft Teams\nStatus: Connected\nOAuth: Valid\n\nGoogle Meet\nStatus: Error\nLast Error: Authentication Failed\n\nSupport agents could inspect:\n\nUser\n ↓\nIntegrations\n ↓\nZoom\n ↓\nConnection Status\n ↓\nLast Successful Operation\n ↓\nLast Error\n\nSensitive OAuth tokens should never be directly displayed in the Admin Console.\n\nThe portal should show metadata such as validity and expiration status, not secrets.\n\n9. Phase 6 – Support Center\n\nThe Support Center connects different Admin modules.\n\nFor example:\n\nCustomer reports issue\n\n        ↓\n\nSearch customer\n\n        ↓\n\nView account\n\n        ↓\n\nFind event\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck event status\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck integrations\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck system health\n\n        ↓\n\nReview audit timeline\n\n        ↓\n\nIdentify problem\n\nThis creates a centralized troubleshooting workflow.\n\nInstead of:\n\nSupport\n   ↓\nDeveloper\n   ↓\nMongoDB Compass\n   ↓\nServer Logs\n   ↓\nRedis\n   ↓\nFind Problem\n\nwe move toward:\n\nSupport\n   ↓\nAdmin Console\n   ↓\nFind Problem\n\nThis is one of the biggest benefits of building the Admin Console.\n\n10. Phase 7 – Platform Analytics\n\nThe existing IEP analytics focuses primarily on individual events.\n\nAdmin Analytics should provide platform-wide metrics.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganizations\n\nTotal Users\n\nDaily Active Users\n\nMonthly Active Users\n\nEvents Created\n\nLive Events\n\nParticipants\n\nPoll Responses\n\nSurvey Responses\n\nAI Requests\n\nAdditional metrics could include:\n\nMost Used Activity\n\nPoll\nQuiz\nQ&A\nSurvey\nWord Cloud\n\nMost Used Integration\n\nZoom\nTeams\nGoogle Meet\n\nThis helps the team understand how customers are actually using the platform.\n\n11. Phase 8 – AI Operations\n\nSince IEP already includes AI Studio and AI-generated content, AI usage should eventually have its own operational dashboard.\n\nIt could show:\n\nAI Operations\n\nRequests Today\n\nRequests This Month\n\nSuccessful Requests\n\nFailed Requests\n\nEstimated Usage/Cost\n\nTop AI Features\n\nTop Organizations by Usage\n\nThis will help detect:\n\nUnexpected usage spikes.\nAPI failures.\nRate-limit problems.\nCustomers consuming excessive resources.\n12. Phase 9 – Audit Logging\n\nEvery sensitive administrative operation should create an immutable audit record.\n\nFor example:\n\nAdmin\nAyush\n\nAction\nUSER_SUSPENDED\n\nTarget\nUser #123\n\nReason\nTerms violation\n\nTimestamp\n2026-07-16 10:30\n\nActions worth auditing include:\n\nUser suspension.\nUser reactivation.\nOrganization changes.\nEvent termination.\nPlan changes.\nFeature flag changes.\nAdmin login.\nSupport access to sensitive account information.\n\nThe Audit Log interface should support filtering by:\n\nAdmin\n\nUser\n\nOrganization\n\nEvent\n\nAction\n\nDate\n\nSeverity\n\nThis is especially important if IEP later serves enterprise customers.\n\n13. Phase 10 – Feature Flags\n\nFeature flags can allow us to control features without deploying new code.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganization: ABC Corporation\n\nAI Studio            Enabled\n\nAdvanced Analytics   Enabled\n\nSurvey               Enabled\n\nZoom                  Enabled\n\nTeams                 Disabled\n\nGoogle Meet           Enabled\n\nFeature flags could operate at different levels:\n\nGlobal\n\nOrganization\n\nUser\n\nThis allows gradual feature rollout and enterprise-specific configurations.\n\n14. Phase 11 – System Health\n\nThe Admin Console can eventually provide operational visibility.\n\nFor example:\n\nSystem Health\n\nAPI                 Healthy\n\nMongoDB             Healthy\n\nRedis               Healthy\n\nSocket.IO           Healthy\n\nAI Provider         Healthy\n\nZoom                Healthy\n\nTeams               Healthy\n\nGoogle Meet         Degraded\n\nThis does not need to replace professional observability platforms. Instead, it should provide support teams with a simplified operational view.\n\nDetailed engineering logs and infrastructure monitoring should remain in dedicated observability systems.\n\n15. Impersonation – Implement Carefully\n\nThe original proposal includes:\n\n\"Log in as this user.\"\n\nThis is useful but also one of the highest-risk features in the entire Admin Console.\n\nI would not include it in the MVP.\n\nInitially, support agents should be able to inspect:\n\nUser\n\nEvents\n\nConfiguration\n\nIntegrations\n\nUsage\n\nAudit History\n\nIf impersonation becomes necessary later, it should use a temporary, restricted support session.\n\nFor example:\n\nSupport Agent\n\n↓\n\nRequest Impersonation\n\n↓\n\nProvide Reason\n\n↓\n\nCreate Temporary Session\n\n↓\n\nRead-Only by Default\n\n↓\n\nSession Automatically Expires\n\n↓\n\nAudit Log Created\n\nThis prevents support staff from silently performing actions as customers.\n\n16. Recommended Implementation Roadmap\n\nI would prioritize development as follows:\n\nStage\tScope\tPriority\nFoundation\tAdmin App + Authentication + RBAC\tCritical\nMVP\tDashboard + User Search + Event Search\tCritical\nSupport\tEvent Diagnostics + Integration Diagnostics\tHigh\nEnterprise\tOrganization Management\tHigh\nGovernance\tAudit Logs + Moderation\tHigh\nIntelligence\tPlatform Analytics + AI Operations\tMedium\nOperations\tSystem Health\tMedium\nCommercial\tPlans + Billing\tFuture\nPlatform Control\tFeature Flags\tFuture\nAdvanced Support\tSecure Impersonation\tFuture\n\nThis approach avoids trying to build everything at once.\n\n17. Recommended MVP\n\nFor the first usable version, I would build only:\n\nAdmin Console MVP\n\nAuthentication & RBAC\n        │\n        ├── Dashboard\n        │\n        ├── User Search\n        │\n        ├── User Details\n        │\n        ├── Event Search\n        │\n        ├── Event Diagnostics\n        │\n        ├── Integration Diagnostics\n        │\n        └── Audit Logs\n\nThis directly addresses Suman Sir's requirement of an Admin App for client support.\n\nOrganizations, billing, feature flags, AI cost management, advanced moderation, and impersonation can come later.\n\n18. Key Decisions Before Implementation\n\nBefore development starts, I recommend resolving four architectural decisions.\n\nAuthentication: Decide whether internal admins use the existing Auth0 tenant or a dedicated employee authentication system.\n\nAuthorization: Decide whether the initial model is simply host/admin or a more granular permissions model.\n\nAdmin UI: Decide whether to reuse the existing IEP design system or use an admin-oriented framework. Since you already have a developed design system, I would initially reuse it to maintain consistency and avoid introducing another major dependency.\n\nOrganizations: Determine whether the current data model already supports multi-tenancy properly. If not, organization architecture should be designed before building organization management.\n\nFinal Proposed Direction\n\nThe Admin Console should not simply be another dashboard. It should become the internal client-support and operations layer of IEP.\n\nThe most important initial workflow should be:\n\nCustomer reports problem\n        ↓\nSupport searches customer\n        ↓\nSupport identifies organization\n        ↓\nSupport finds affected event\n        ↓\nSupport checks event state\n        ↓\nSupport checks integrations\n        ↓\nSupport identifies error\n        ↓\nSupport performs authorized action\n        ↓\nAction recorded in Audit Log\n        ↓\nIssue resolved\n\n\nwhat you think abot this\n</USER_REQUEST>\n<ADDITIONAL_METADATA>\nThe current local time is: 2026-07-17T18:45:30+05:30.\n\nThe user's current state is as follows:\nOther open documents:\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\web\\src\\app\\support\\page.tsx (LANGUAGE_TSX)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\api\\src\\analytics\\templates\\report-template.ts (LANGUAGE_TYPESCRIPT)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\web\\.env.local (LANGUAGE_UNSPECIFIED)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\web\\src\\app\\api\\powerpoint\\link-presentation\\route.ts (LANGUAGE_TYPESCRIPT)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\api\\src\\powerpoint\\powerpoint.module.ts (LANGUAGE_TYPESCRIPT)\n</ADDITIONAL_METADATA>"}

No code has been modified.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Monorepo Audit Summary\n\n| Area | Finding |\n|---|---|\n| **Turborepo** | `turbo.json` uses `apps/*` glob — `apps/admin` is auto-discovered. No turbo.json changes needed. |\n| **Auth** | `@auth0/nextjs-auth0 v3` in `apps/web`. The `withApiAuthRequired` proxy pattern is the established way to call the NestJS API from Next.js. We will replicate this exact pattern in `apps/admin`. |\n| **RBAC (API)** | `JwtAuthGuard` (passport-jwt + JWKS-RSA) + `RolesGuard` + `@Roles('admin')` decorator already exists and is proven. The `users` collection already stores `role: 'host' | 'admin'`. **Backend is already the RBAC source of truth.** |\n| **Admin Module** | `apps/api/src/admin/` exists with `admin.controller.ts` (only `GET /admin/stats`) and `admin.module.ts`. **No `admin.service.ts` yet.** |\n| **Design System** | Rich Pulse design system lives in `apps/web/src/` — tokens (colors, typography, spacing, motion, elevation), UI primitives (Button, Card, Badge, SearchBar, MetricCard, PageHeader, Input, etc.), layout (`DashboardShell`). **All are internal to `apps/web` — not yet a shared package.** |\n| **API Proxy** | `apps/web/src/app/api/proxy/[...path]/route.ts` — a `withApiAuthRequired` handler that appends the Auth0 Bearer token and proxies to NestJS. We will create an identical route in `apps/admin`. |\n| **Packages** | `@iep/types` (Zod schemas for User, Event, etc.) and `@iep/config` (shared ESLint/tsconfig) are both available as workspace deps. |\n| **Health** | `GET /health`, `GET /live`, `GET /ready` exist in NestJS — no auth required. Admin can call these freely. |\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Architectural Decisions\n\n### Design System — Copy, Don't Move (Yet)\nThe Pulse design system (tokens, UI primitives, `DashboardShell`) is currently embedded inside `apps/web/src`. **We will not move it to a shared package in Phase 1** — that is a significant refactor that risks breaking `apps/web`. Instead we will **copy** the minimum required files into `apps/admin/src/`. In a future sprint, we can extract to `packages/ui`.\n\nFiles we will copy into `apps/admin`:\n- All token CSS files (`styles/pulse/tokens/*.css`)\n- The `cn()` utility (`lib/utils.ts`)\n- Core UI primitives: `button.tsx`, `card.tsx`, `badge.tsx`, `input.tsx`, `search-bar.tsx`, `metric-card.tsx`, `page-header.tsx`, `section-header.tsx`\n- Brand marks: `components/pulse/wordmark.tsx` (references `/public/brand/*.svg`)\n- Public brand SVGs: `pulse-wordmark.svg`, `pulse-wordmark-dark.svg`, `pulse-logomark.svg`\n\n### Auth0 — Same Tenant, Same Pattern\nWe will reuse the existing Auth0 tenant and the same `AUTH0_AUDIENCE`, `AUTH0_ISSUER_BASE_URL` etc. `apps/admin` will have its own Auth0 callback URL (`http://localhost:3001/api/auth/callback` in dev). No additional Auth0 application setup is strictly required — we create a new Auth0 Application (type: Regular Web Application) pointing at the admin port.\n\n### Frontend RBAC — Check After Login\nThe `apps/admin` middleware will:\n1. Check if the user is logged in (Auth0 session). Redirect to `/login` if not.\n2. Fetch `GET /admin/stats` (or a new `GET /admin/me` endpoint) on the home page. If the NestJS API returns **403**, the frontend shows an \"Access Denied\" page.\n\nThe backend is the **actual enforcer**. The frontend role check is only for UX — to show a friendly error instead of a cryptic 403 when a non-admin accidentally lands on the admin URL.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Files to be Created\n\n### `apps/admin` — New Next.js Application\n\n```\napps/admin/\n├── package.json\n├── tsconfig.json\n├── next.config.mjs\n├── tailwind.config.ts\n├── postcss.config.cjs\n├── .env.local.example\n├── public/\n│   └── brand/\n│       ├── pulse-wordmark.svg          (copy from apps/web/public/brand/)\n│       ├── pulse-wordmark-dark.svg     (copy)\n│       └── pulse-logomark.svg          (copy)\n└── src/\n    ├── styles/\n    │   └── pulse/\n    │       └── tokens/\n    │           ├── colors.css          (copy from apps/web)\n    │           ├── typography.css      (copy)\n    │           ├── spacing.css         (copy)\n    │           ├── elevation.css       (copy)\n    │           ├── motion.css          (copy)\n    │           └── fonts.css           (copy)\n    ├── lib/\n    │   ├── utils.ts                    (copy cn() from apps/web)\n    │   └── admin-api.ts               [NEW] — typed fetch wrapper for /api/proxy\n    ├── components/\n    │   ├── ui/\n    │   │   ├── button.tsx             (copy)\n    │   │   ├── card.tsx               (copy)\n    │   │   ├── badge.tsx              (copy)\n    │   │   ├── input.tsx              (copy)\n    │   │   ├── search-bar.tsx         (copy)\n    │   │   ├── metric-card.tsx        (copy)\n    │   │   ├── page-header.tsx        (copy)\n    │   │   └── section-header.tsx Security Implications\n\n| Risk | Mitigation |\n|---|---|\n| Non-admin user accesses `/home` | NestJS returns 403 on all `/admin/*` routes. Frontend redirects to `/access-denied`. |\n| Token theft via XSS | Auth0 SDK stores tokens in HttpOnly cookies. The proxy never exposes the token to client-side JS. |\n| Admin app misconfigured to share `apps/web` Auth0 client | A **new, separate Auth0 Application** is required for `apps/admin`. Credentials must never be shared. |\n| Sensitive OAuth tokens visible | Phase 1 has no token display. Phase 5 (Integrations) will show only metadata (status, expiry) — never raw tokens. |\n| CORS between admin and API | The NestJS API already has `WEB_ORIGIN` for CORS. We must add the admin origin to the API's CORS config. |\n\n### Required API CORS Change\n`apps/api/src/main.ts` must allow `http://localhost:3001` (admin dev) and the production admin URL.\n\n---\n\n## 9. This phase introduces a highly secure, immutable Audit Log to provide accountability for all powerful administrative mutations (starting with the \"Force End Session\" capability introduced in Phase 4).\n\n## Data Model & Schema\n\nWe will create a new MongoDB collection strictly for audit trails: `AdminAuditLog` (`apps/api/src/admin/audit-log.schema.ts`).\n\n**Schema Fields:**\n- `adminId` (String / ObjectId): The authenticated admin who performed the action.\n- `adminEmail` (String): Captured at the time of the event for historical accuracy if the admin account is later deleted.\n- `actionType` (Enum): E.g., `FORCE_END_EVENT`, `FORCE_UNLINK_INTEGRATION` (future).\n- `targetResourceType` (Enum): E.g., `Event`, `User`.\n- `targetResourceId` (String): The Mongo ID or external ID of the affected resource.\n- `reason` (String, Optional): Admin-provided justification for the action.\n- `metadata` (Object, Optional): Safe contextual data (e.g., event name, socket count disconnected). **Must never contain credentials or PII.**\n- `timestamp` (Date): Automatically generated by Mongoose `timestamps`.\n\n## Failure Handling Strategy\n**\"Fail Open\" vs \"Fail Closed\":**\nIf the core action (e.g., Force End Event) succeeds, but the database insert for the Audit Log fails (e.g., transient network error), what happens?\n- **Recommendation (Fail Open):** We will execute the core action, catch the audit log failure, log a critical error to the application logger (e.g., stdout/CloudWatch), but **not** roll back the core action. Forcing an event to end is typically an emergency action; it should not be blocked by an audit side-effect failing.\n\n## Security & Protection\n- **Immutability:** The backend API will **only** expose a `GET` endpoint for the audit logs. There will be no `PUT`, `PATCH`, or `DELETE` endpoints. Admins cannot delete their own tracks.\n- **Data Retention:** Since audit logs grow perpetually, we should consider a MongoDB TTL index (e.g., 90 or 365 days) or cold storage offloading. For this MVP, we will retain logs indefinitely.\n\n## Proposed Changes\n\n### Backend APIs (`apps/api/src/admin`)\n\n#### [NEW] This phase introduces a highly secure, immutable Audit Log to provide accountability for all powerful administrative mutations (starting with the \"Force End Session\" capability introduced in Phase 4).\n\n## Data Model & Schema\n\nWe will create a new MongoDB collection strictly for audit trails: `AdminAuditLog` (`apps/api/src/admin/audit-log.schema.ts`).\n\n**Schema Fields:**\n- `adminId` (String / ObjectId): The authenticated admin who performed the action.\n- `adminEmail` (String): Captured at the time of the event for historical accuracy if the admin account is later deleted.\n- `actionType` (Enum): E.g., `FORCE_END_EVENT`, `FORCE_UNLINK_INTEGRATION` (future).\n- `targetResourceType` (Enum): E.g., `Event`, `User`.\n- `targetResourceId` (String): The Mongo ID or external ID of the affected resource.\n- `reason` (String, Optional): Admin-provided justification for the action.\n- `metadata` (Object, Optional): Safe contextual data (e.g., event name, socket count disconnected). **Must never contain credentials or PII.**\n- `timestamp` (Date): Automatically generated by Mongoose `timestamps`.\n\n## Failure Handling Strategy\n**\"Fail Open\" vs \"Fail Closed\":**\nIf the core action (e.g., Force End Event) succeeds, but the database insert for the Audit Log fails (e.g., transient network error), what happens?\n- **Recommendation (Fail Open):** We will execute the core action, catch the audit log failure, log a critical error to the application logger (e.g., stdout/CloudWatch), but **not** roll back the core action. Forcing an event to end is typically an emergency action; it should not be blocked by an audit side-effect failing.\n\n## Security & Protection\n- **Immutability:** The backend API will **only** expose a `GET` endpoint for the audit logs. There will be no `PUT`, `PATCH`, or `DELETE` endpoints. Admins cannot delete their own tracks.\n- **Data Retention:** Since audit logs grow perpetually, we should consider a MongoDB TTL index (e.g., 90 or 365 days) or cold storage offloading. For this MVP, we will retain logs indefinitely.\n\n## Proposed Changes\n\n### Backend APIs (`apps/api/src/admin`)\n\n#### [NEW] Phase 6 – Support Center\n\nThe Support Center connects different Admin modules.\n\nFor example:\n\nCustomer reports issue\n\n        ↓\n\nSearch customer\n\n        ↓\n\nView account\n\n        ↓\n\nFind event\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck event status\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck integrations\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck system health\n\n        ↓\n\nReview audit timeline\n\n        ↓\n\nIdentify problem\n\nThis creates a centralized troubleshooting workflow.\n\nInstead of:\n\nSupport\n   ↓\nDeveloper\n   ↓\nMongoDB Compass\n   ↓\nServer Logs\n   ↓\nRedis\n   ↓\nFind Problem\n\nwe move toward:\n\nSupport\n   ↓\nAdmin Console\n   ↓\nFind Problem\n\nThis is one of the biggest benefits of building the Admin Console.\n\n10. Phase 7 – Platform Analytics\n\nThe existing IEP analytics focuses primarily on individual events.\n\nAdmin Analytics should provide platform-wide metrics.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganizations\n\nTotal Users\n\nDaily Active Users\n\nMonthly Active Users\n\nEvents Created\n\nLive Events\n\nParticipants\n\nPoll Responses\n\nSurvey Responses\n\nAI Requests\n\nAdditional metrics could include:\n\nMost Used Activity\n\nPoll\nQuiz\nQ&A\nSurvey\nWord Cloud\n\nMost Used Integration\n\nZoom\nTeams\nGoogle Meet\n\nThis helps the team understand how customers are actually using the platform.\n\n11. Phase 8 – AI Operations\n\nSince IEP already includes AI Studio and AI-generated content, AI usage should eventually have its own operational dashboard.\n\nIt could show:\n\nAI Operations\n\nRequests Today\n\nRequests This Month\n\nSuccessful Requests\n\nFailed Requests\n\nEstimated Usage/Cost\n\nTop AI Features\n\nTop Organizations by Usage\n\nThis will help detect:\n\nUnexpected usage spikes.\nAPI failures.\nRate-limit problems.\nCustomers consuming excessive resources.\n12. Phase 9 – Audit Logging\n\nEvery sensitive administrative operation should create an immutable audit record.\n\nFor example:\n\nAdmin\nAyush\n\nAction\nUSER_SUSPENDED\n\nTarget\nUser #123\n\nReason\nTerms violation\n\nTimestamp\n2026-07-16 10:30\n\nActions worth auditing include:\n\nUser suspension.\nUser reactivation.\nOrganization changes.\nEvent termination.\nPlan changes.\nFeature flag changes.\nAdmin login.\nSupport access to sensitive account information.\n\nThe Audit Log interface should support filtering by:\n\nAdmin\n\nUser\n\nOrganization\n\nEvent\n\nAction\n\nDate\n\nSeverity\n\nThis is especially important if IEP later serves enterprise customers.\n\n13. Phase 10 – Feature Flags\n\nFeature flags can allow us to control features without deploying new code.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganization: ABC Corporation\n\nAI Studio            Enabled\n\nAdvanced Analytics   Enabled\n\nSurvey               Enabled\n\nZoom                  Enabled\n\nTeams                 Disabled\n\nGoogle Meet           Enabled\n\nFeature flags could operate at different levels:\n\nGlobal\n\nOrganization\n\nUser\n\nThis allows gradual feature rollout and enterprise-specific configurations.\n\n14. Phase 11 – System Health\n\nThe Admin Console can eventually provide operational visibility.\n\nFor example:\n\nSystem Health\n\nAPI                 Healthy\n\nMongoDB             Healthy\n\nRedis               Healthy\n\nSocket.IO           Healthy\n\nAI Provider         Healthy\n\nZoom                Healthy\n\nTeams               Healthy\n\nGoogle Meet         Degraded\n\nThis does not need to replace professional observability platforms. Instead, it should provide support teams with a simplified operational view.\n\nDetailed engineering logs and infrastructure monitoring should remain in dedicated observability systems.\n\n15. Impersonation – Implement Carefully\n\nThe original proposal includes:\n\n\"Log in as this user.\"\n\nThis is useful but also one of the highest-risk features in the entire Admin Console.\n\nI would not include it in the MVP.\n\nInitially, support agents should be able to inspect:\n\nUser\n\nEvents\n\nConfiguration\n\nIntegrations\n\nUsage\n\nAudit History\n\nIf impersonation becomes necessary later, it should use a temporary, restricted support session.\n\nFor example:\n\nSupport Agent\n\n↓\n\nRequest Impersonation\n\n↓\n\nProvide Reason\n\n↓\n\nCreate Temporary Session\n\n↓\n\nRead-Only by Default\n\n↓\n\nSession Automatically Expires\n\n↓\n\nAudit Log Created\n\nThis prevents support staff from silently performing actions as customers.\n\n16. If not, organization architecture should be designed before building organization management.\n\nFinal Proposed Direction\n\nThe Admin Console should not simply be another dashboard. {"step_index":2282,"source":"MODEL","type":"RUN_COMMAND","status":"DONE","created_at":"2026-07-20T03:16:53Z","content":"Created At: 2026-07-20T03:16:53Z\nCompleted At: 2026-07-20T03:16:54Z\n\n\t\t\t\tThe command completed successfully.\n\t\t\t\tOutput:\n\t\t\t\t<truncated 1 lines>\n\nBecause IEP integrates with:\n\nZoom\nMicrosoft Teams\nGoogle Meet\n\nintegration troubleshooting should have its own module.\n\nThe Admin Console could display:\n\nIntegration Health\n\nZoom\nStatus: Connected\nOAuth: Valid\nLast Sync: 10 minutes ago\n\nMicrosoft Teams\nStatus: Connected\nOAuth: Valid\n\nGoogle Meet\nStatus: Error\nLast Error: Authentication Failed\n\nSupport agents could inspect:\n\nUser\n ↓\nIntegrations\n ↓\nZoom\n ↓\nConnection Status\n ↓\nLast Successful Operation\n ↓\nLast Error\n\nSensitive OAuth tokens should never be directly displayed in the Admin Console.\n\nThe portal should show metadata such as validity and expiration status, not secrets.\n\n9. Phase 6 – Support Center\n\nThe Support Center connects different Admin modules.\n\nFor example:\n\nCustomer reports issue\n\n        ↓\n\nSearch customer\n\n        ↓\n\nView account\n\n        ↓\n\nFind event\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck event status\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck integrations\n\n        ↓\n\nCheck system health\n\n        ↓\n\nReview audit timeline\n\n        ↓\n\nIdentify problem\n\nThis creates a centralized troubleshooting workflow.\n\nInstead of:\n\nSupport\n   ↓\nDeveloper\n   ↓\nMongoDB Compass\n   ↓\nServer Logs\n   ↓\nRedis\n   ↓\nFind Problem\n\nwe move toward:\n\nSupport\n   ↓\nAdmin Console\n   ↓\nFind Problem\n\nThis is one of the biggest benefits of building the Admin Console.\n\n10. Phase 7 – Platform Analytics\n\nThe existing IEP analytics focuses primarily on individual events.\n\nAdmin Analytics should provide platform-wide metrics.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganizations\n\nTotal Users\n\nDaily Active Users\n\nMonthly Active Users\n\nEvents Created\n\nLive Events\n\nParticipants\n\nPoll Responses\n\nSurvey Responses\n\nAI Requests\n\nAdditional metrics could include:\n\nMost Used Activity\n\nPoll\nQuiz\nQ&A\nSurvey\nWord Cloud\n\nMost Used Integration\n\nZoom\nTeams\nGoogle Meet\n\nThis helps the team understand how customers are actually using the platform.\n\n11. Phase 8 – AI Operations\n\nSince IEP already includes AI Studio and AI-generated content, AI usage should eventually have its own operational dashboard.\n\nIt could show:\n\nAI Operations\n\nRequests Today\n\nRequests This Month\n\nSuccessful Requests\n\nFailed Requests\n\nEstimated Usage/Cost\n\nTop AI Features\n\nTop Organizations by Usage\n\nThis will help detect:\n\nUnexpected usage spikes.\nAPI failures.\nRate-limit problems.\nCustomers consuming excessive resources.\n12. Phase 9 – Audit Logging\n\nEvery sensitive administrative operation should create an immutable audit record.\n\nFor example:\n\nAdmin\nAyush\n\nAction\nUSER_SUSPENDED\n\nTarget\nUser #123\n\nReason\nTerms violation\n\nTimestamp\n2026-07-16 10:30\n\nActions worth auditing include:\n\nUser suspension.\nUser reactivation.\nOrganization changes.\nEvent termination.\nPlan changes.\nFeature flag changes.\nAdmin login.\nSupport access to sensitive account information.\n\nThe Audit Log interface should support filtering by:\n\nAdmin\n\nUser\n\nOrganization\n\nEvent\n\nAction\n\nDate\n\nSeverity\n\nThis is especially important if IEP later serves enterprise customers.\n\n13. Phase 10 – Feature Flags\n\nFeature flags can allow us to control features without deploying new code.\n\nFor example:\n\nOrganization: ABC Corporation\n\nAI Studio            Enabled\n\nAdvanced Analytics   Enabled\n\nSurvey               Enabled\n\nZoom                  Enabled\n\nTeams                 Disabled\n\nGoogle Meet           Enabled\n\nFeature flags could operate at different levels:\n\nGlobal\n\nOrganization\n\nUser\n\nThis allows gradual feature rollout and enterprise-specific configurations.\n\n14. Phase 11 – System Health\n\nThe Admin Console can eventually provide operational visibility.\n\nFor example:\n\nSystem Health\n\nAPI                 Healthy\n\nMongoDB             Healthy\n\nRedis               Healthy\n\nSocket.IO           Healthy\n\nAI Provider         Healthy\n\nZoom                Healthy\n\nTeams               Healthy\n\nGoogle Meet         Degraded\n\nThis does not need to replace professional observability platforms. Instead, it should provide support teams with a simplified operational view.\n\nDetailed engineering logs and infrastructure monitoring should remain in dedicated observability systems.\n\n15. Impersonation – Implement Carefully\n\nThe original proposal includes:\n\n\"Log in as this user.\"\n\nThis is useful but also one of the highest-risk features in the entire Admin Console.\n\nI would not include it in the MVP.\n\nInitially, support agents should be able to inspect:\n\nUser\n\nEvents\n\nConfiguration\n\nIntegrations\n\nUsage\n\nAudit History\n\nIf impersonation becomes necessary later, it should use a temporary, restricted support session.\n\nFor example:\n\nSupport Agent\n\n↓\n\nRequest Impersonation\n\n↓\n\nProvide Reason\n\n↓\n\nCreate Temporary Session\n\n↓\n\nRead-Only by Default\n\n↓\n\nSession Automatically Expires\n\n↓\n\nAudit Log Created\n\nThis prevents support staff from silently performing actions as customers.\n\n16. Recommended Implementation Roadmap\n\nI would prioritize development as follows:\n\nStage\tScope\tPriority\nFoundation\tAdmin App + Authentication + RBAC\tCritical\nMVP\tDashboard + User Search + Event Search\tCritical\nSupport\tEvent Diagnostics + Integration Diagnostics\tHigh\nEnterprise\tOrganization Management\tHigh\nGovernance\tAudit Logs + Moderation\tHigh\nIntelligence\tPlatform Analytics + AI Operations\tMedium\nOperations\tSystem Health\tMedium\nCommercial\tPlans + Billing\tFuture\nPlatform Control\tFeature Flags\tFuture\nAdvanced Support\tSecure Impersonation\tFuture\n\nThis approach avoids trying to build everything at once.\n\n17. Recommended MVP\n\nFor the first usable version, I would build only:\n\nAdmin Console MVP\n\nAuthentication & RBAC\n        │\n        ├── Dashboard\n        │\n        ├── User Search\n        │\n        ├── User Details\n        │\n        ├── Event Search\n        │\n        ├── Event Diagnostics\n        │\n        ├── Integration Diagnostics\n        │\n        └── Audit Logs\n\nThis directly addresses Suman Sir's requirement of an Admin App for client support.\n\nOrganizations, billing, feature flags, AI cost management, advanced moderation, and impersonation can come later.\n\n18. Key Decisions Before Implementation\n\nBefore development starts, I recommend resolving four architectural decisions.\n\nAuthentication: Decide whether internal admins use the existing Auth0 tenant or a dedicated employee authentication system.\n\nAuthorization: Decide whether the initial model is simply host/admin or a more granular permissions model.\n\nAdmin UI: Decide whether to reuse the existing IEP design system or use an admin-oriented framework. Since you already have a developed design system, I would initially reuse it to maintain consistency and avoid introducing another major dependency.\n\nOrganizations: Determine whether the current data model already supports multi-tenancy properly. If not, organization architecture should be designed before building organization management.\n\nFinal Proposed Direction\n\nThe Admin Console should not simply be another dashboard. It should become the internal client-support and operations layer of IEP.\n\nThe most important initial workflow should be:\n\nCustomer reports problem\n        ↓\nSupport searches customer\n        ↓\nSupport identifies organization\n        ↓\nSupport finds affected event\n        ↓\nSupport checks event state\n        ↓\nSupport checks integrations\n        ↓\nSupport identifies error\n        ↓\nSupport performs authorized action\n        ↓\nAction recorded in Audit Log\n        ↓\nIssue resolved\n\n\nwhat you think abot this\n</USER_REQUEST>\n<ADDITIONAL_METADATA>\nThe current local time is: 2026-07-17T18:45:30+05:30.\n\nThe user's current state is as follows:\nOther open documents:\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\web\\src\\app\\support\\page.tsx (LANGUAGE_TSX)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\api\\src\\analytics\\templates\\report-template.ts (LANGUAGE_TYPESCRIPT)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\web\\.env.local (LANGUAGE_UNSPECIFIED)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\web\\src\\app\\api\\powerpoint\\link-presentation\\route.ts (LANGUAGE_TYPESCRIPT)\n- c:\\Users\\ayush\\Downloads\\interactive-engagement-app\\apps\\api\\src\\powerpoint\\powerpoint.module.ts (LANGUAGE_TYPESCRIPT)\n</ADDITIONAL_METADATA>\n\n"}
